<li>6. BloodyElbow.com (SB Nation)</li>
<li>7. Mixedmartialarts.com</li>
<li>8. <a href="/wiki/ESPN.com" title="ESPN.com">ESPN.com</a>/mma</li>
<li>9. MMAWeekly.com</li>
<li>10. Lowkickmma.com</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fighter_development">Fighter development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Fighter development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
As a result of an increased number of competitors, organized training camps, information sharing, and modern <a href="/wiki/Kinesiology" title="Kinesiology">kinesiology</a>, the understanding of the effectiveness of various strategies has been greatly improved. UFC commentator <a href="/wiki/Joe_Rogan" title="Joe Rogan">Joe Rogan</a> claimed that martial arts evolved more in the ten years following 1993 than in the preceding 700 years combined.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:23em;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"During his reign atop the sport in the late 1990s he was the prototype — he could strike with the best strikers; he could grapple with the best grapplers; his endurance was second to none. "</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— describing UFC champion <a href="/wiki/Frank_Shamrock" title="Frank Shamrock">Frank Shamrock</a>'s early dominance<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>The high profile of modern MMA promotions such as UFC and Pride has fostered an accelerated development of the sport. The early 1990s saw a wide variety of traditional styles competing in the sport.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> However, early competition saw varying levels of success among disparate styles.
In the early 1990s, practitioners of grappling based styles such as <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_jiu-jitsu" title="Brazilian jiu-jitsu">Brazilian jiu-jitsu</a> dominated competition in the United States. Practitioners of striking based arts such as <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a>, who were unfamiliar with submission grappling, proved to be unprepared to deal with its <a href="/wiki/Submission_hold" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission hold">submission techniques</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UFCHISTORYHSW1_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UFCHISTORYHSW1-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> As competitions became more and more common, those with a base in striking arts became more competitive as they cross-trained in styles based around <a href="/wiki/Takedown_(grappling)" title="Takedown (grappling)">takedowns</a> and submission holds.<sup id="cite_ref-UFCHISTORYHSW1_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UFCHISTORYHSW1-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Likewise, those from the varying grappling styles added striking techniques to their arsenal. This increase of <a href="/wiki/Cross-training" title="Cross-training">cross-training</a> resulted in fighters becoming increasingly multidimensional and well-rounded in their skill-sets.
</p><p>The new hybridization of fighting styles can be seen in the technique of "ground and pound" developed by wrestling-based UFC pioneers such as <a href="/wiki/Dan_Severn" title="Dan Severn">Dan Severn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Frye" title="Don Frye">Don Frye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Coleman" title="Mark Coleman">Mark Coleman</a>. These wrestlers realized the need for the incorporation of strikes on the ground as well as on the feet, and incorporated ground striking into their grappling-based styles. Mark Coleman stated at UFC 14 that his strategy was to "Ground him and pound him", which may be the first televised use of the term.
</p><p>Since the late 1990s, both strikers and grapplers have been successful at MMA, though it is rare to see any fighter who is not schooled in both striking and grappling arts reach the highest levels of competition.
</p><p>The greatest MMA fighter of all time is considered by experts, fighters and fans to be either heavyweight <a href="/wiki/Fedor_Emelianenko" title="Fedor Emelianenko">Fedor Emelianenko</a> or middleweight <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Silva" title="Anderson Silva">Anderson Silva</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> UFC <a href="/wiki/Color_commentator" title="Color commentator">color commentator</a> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Rogan" title="Joe Rogan">Joe Rogan</a> responded to a fan's question: "Joe, is Fedor the Greatest Of All Time? It's him or Anderson, and I could see the argument going either way honestly. Both guys have had truly magical moments in competition against some of the best in the world."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rules">Rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_rules" title="Mixed martial arts rules">Mixed martial arts rules</a></div>
<p>The rules for modern mixed martial arts competitions have changed significantly since the early days of <a href="/wiki/Vale_tudo" title="Vale tudo">vale tudo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Shoot_wrestling" title="Shoot wrestling">shoot wrestling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UFC_1" title="UFC 1">UFC 1</a>, and even more from the historic style of <a href="/wiki/Pankration" title="Pankration">pankration</a>. As the knowledge of fighting techniques spread among fighters and spectators, it became clear that the original minimalist rule systems needed to be amended.<sup id="cite_ref-Warriors_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warriors-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
The main motivations for these rule changes were protection of the health of the fighters, the desire to shed the perception of "barbarism and lawlessness", and to be recognized as a legitimate sport.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The new rules included the introduction of <a href="/wiki/MMA_weight_classes" class="mw-redirect" title="MMA weight classes">weight classes</a>; as knowledge about submissions spread, differences in weight had become a significant factor. There are nine different weight classes in the <a href="/wiki/Unified_Rules_of_Mixed_Martial_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Rules of Mixed Martial Arts">Unified Rules of Mixed Martial Arts</a>. These nine weight classes include <a href="/wiki/Flyweight_(MMA)" title="Flyweight (MMA)">flyweight</a> (up to 125&#160;lb&#160;/&#160;56.7&#160;kg), <a href="/wiki/Bantamweight_(MMA)" title="Bantamweight (MMA)">bantamweight</a> (up to 135&#160;lb&#160;/ 61.2&#160;kg), <a href="/wiki/Featherweight_(MMA)" title="Featherweight (MMA)">featherweight</a> (up to 145&#160;lb&#160;/ 65.8&#160;kg), <a href="/wiki/Lightweight_(MMA)" title="Lightweight (MMA)">lightweight</a> (up to 155&#160;lb&#160;/ 70.3&#160;kg), <a href="/wiki/Welterweight_(MMA)" title="Welterweight (MMA)">welterweight</a> (up to 170&#160;lb&#160;/ 77.1&#160;kg), <a href="/wiki/Middleweight_(MMA)" title="Middleweight (MMA)">middleweight</a> (up to 185&#160;lb&#160;/ 83.9&#160;kg), <a href="/wiki/Light_heavyweight_(MMA)" title="Light heavyweight (MMA)">light heavyweight</a> (up to 205&#160;lb&#160;/ 93.0&#160;kg), <a href="/wiki/Heavyweight_(MMA)" title="Heavyweight (MMA)">heavyweight</a> (up to 265&#160;lb&#160;/ 120.2&#160;kg), and <a href="/wiki/Super_heavyweight_(MMA)" title="Super heavyweight (MMA)">super heavyweight</a> with no upper weight limit.<sup id="cite_ref-njacb_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-njacb-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/MMA_gloves" title="MMA gloves">Small, open-fingered gloves</a> were introduced to protect fists, reduce the occurrence of cuts (and stoppages due to cuts) and encourage fighters to use their hands for striking to allow more captivating matches. Gloves were first made mandatory in Japan's <a href="/wiki/Shooto" title="Shooto">Shooto</a> promotion and were later adopted by the UFC as it developed into a regulated sport. Most professional fights have the fighters wear 4 oz gloves, whereas some jurisdictions require amateurs to wear a slightly heavier 6 oz glove for more protection for the hands and wrists.
</p><p>Time limits were established to avoid long fights with little action where competitors conserved their strength. Matches without time limits also complicated the airing of live events. The time limits in most professional fights are three 5 minute rounds, and championship fights are normally five 5 minute rounds. Similar motivations produced the "stand up" rule, where the referee can stand fighters up if it is perceived that both are resting on the ground or not advancing toward a dominant position.<sup id="cite_ref-Warriors_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warriors-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the U.S., state athletic and boxing commissions have played a crucial role in the introduction of additional rules because they oversee MMA in a similar fashion to boxing. In Japan and most of Europe, there is no regulating authority over competitions, so these organizations have greater freedom in rule development and event structure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Previously, Japan-based organization <a href="/wiki/Pride_Fighting_Championships" title="Pride Fighting Championships">Pride Fighting Championships</a> held an opening 10-minute round followed by two five-minute rounds. Stomps, soccer kicks and knees to the head of a grounded opponent are legal, but elbow strikes to the head are not.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> This rule set is more predominant in the Asian-based organizations as opposed to European and American rules. More recently, Singapore-based organization <a href="/wiki/ONE_Championship" title="ONE Championship">ONE Championship</a> allows soccer kicks and knees to the head of a grounded opponent as well as elbow strikes to the head, but does not allow head stomps.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Victory">Victory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Victory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Victory in a match is normally gained either by the judges' decision after an allotted amount of time has elapsed, a stoppage by the referee (for example if a competitor can not defend himself intelligently) or the fight doctor (due to an injury), a <a href="/wiki/Submission_(combat_sports)" title="Submission (combat sports)">submission</a>, by a competitor's <a href="/wiki/Cornerman" title="Cornerman">cornerman</a> throwing in the towel, or by <a href="/wiki/Knockout" title="Knockout">knockout</a>.
</p><p>Knockout (KO): as soon as a fighter is unable to continue due to legal strikes, his opponent is declared the winner. As MMA rules allow submissions and <a href="/wiki/Ground_and_pound" class="mw-redirect" title="Ground and pound">ground and pound</a>, the fight is stopped to prevent further injury to the fighter.
</p><p>Submission: a fighter may admit defeat during a match by:
</p>
<ul><li>a physical tap on the opponent's body or mat/floor</li>
<li>tapping verbally</li></ul>
<p>Technical Submission: the referee stops the match when the fighter is caught in a submission hold and is in danger of being injured. This can occur when a fighter is choked unconscious, or when a bone has been broken in a submission hold (a broken arm due to a kimura, etc.)
</p><p>Technical Knockout (TKO):
</p>
<ul><li>Referee stoppage: The referee may stop a match in progress if:
<ul><li>a fighter becomes dominant to the point where the opponent cannot intelligently defend themself and is taking excessive damage as a result</li>
<li>a fighter appears to be losing consciousness as he/she is being struck</li>
<li>a fighter appears to have a significant injury such as a cut or a broken bone</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Doctor Stoppage/Cut: the referee will call for a time out if a fighter's ability to continue is in question as a result of apparent injuries, such as a large cut. The ring doctor will inspect the fighter and stop the match if the fighter is deemed unable to continue safely, rendering the opponent the winner. However, if the match is stopped as a result of an injury from illegal actions by the opponent, either a disqualification or no contest will be issued instead.
</p><p>Corner stoppage: a fighter's corner may announce defeat on the fighter's behalf by throwing in the towel during the match in progress or between rounds. This is normally done when a fighter is being beaten to the point where it is dangerous and unnecessary to continue. In some cases, the fighter may be injured.
</p><p>Retirement: a fighter is so dazed or exhausted that he/she cannot physically continue fighting. Usually occurs between rounds.
</p><p>Decision: if the match goes the distance, then the outcome of the bout is determined by three judges. The judging criteria are organization-specific.
</p><p>Forfeit: a fighter or their representative may forfeit a match prior to the beginning of the match, thereby losing the match.
</p><p>Disqualification: a "warning" will be given when a fighter commits a foul or illegal action or does not follow the referee's instruction. Three warnings will result in a disqualification. Moreover, if a fighter is unable to continue due to a deliberate illegal technique from his opponent, the opponent will be disqualified.
</p><p>No Contest: in the event that both fighters commit a violation of the rules, or a fighter is unable to continue due to an injury from an accidental illegal technique, the match will be declared a "No Contest", except in the case of a technical decision in the unified rules. A result can also be overturned to a no contest if the fighter that was originally victorious fails a post fight drug test for banned substances.
</p><p>Technical decision: in the unified rules of MMA, if a fighter is unable to continue due to an accidental illegal technique late in the fight, a technical decision is rendered by the judges based on who is ahead on the judges' scorecards at that time. In a three-round fight, two rounds must be completed for a technical decision to be awarded and in a five-round fight, three rounds must be completed.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fighter_ranking">Fighter ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fighter ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sports_rating_system" title="Sports rating system">Sports rating system</a></div>
<p>MMA fighters are ranked according to their performance and outcome of their fights and level of competition they faced. The most popular and used, ranking portals are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fight_Matrix" title="Fight Matrix">Fight Matrix</a>: Ranks up to 250-500 fighters worldwide for every possible division male and female.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sherdog" title="Sherdog">Sherdog</a>: Ranks top 10 fighters worldwide only for current available UFC divisions. Also used by <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SB_Nation" title="SB Nation">SB Nation</a>: Ranks top 14 fighters worldwide only for male divisions. Also used by <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MMAjunkie.com" title="MMAjunkie.com">MMAjunkie.com</a>: Ranks top 10 fighters worldwide for current UFC available divisions.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a>: Ranks top 15 contenders, UFC signed fighters only, as per UFC divisions. (For example: #2 means the fighter is #3 for the UFC, behind the Champion and the #1)</li>
<li>Tapology: Ranks top 10 fighters worldwide for every possible division.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a>: Ranks top 10 fighters worldwide for current UFC available divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>MMA Rising: Ranks top 10 fighters worldwide in every possible division.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Notable for their <i>Unified Women's Mixed Martial Arts. Rankings</i><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>MMA Weekly: Ranks top 10 male fighters worldwide in every possible division, and P4P for female fighters.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Also used by <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo! Sports">Yahoo! Sports</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bleacher_Report" title="Bleacher Report">Bleacher Report</a>: Ranks top 10 UFC fighters in each division.</li>
<li>Fight! Magazine: Ranks top 5 fighters and only in male divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Ranking MMA: Ranks top 20 male fighters worldwide in each division and also by promotions.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Oddsshark.com: Ranks top 10 fighters worldwide in current UFC divisions.</li>
<li>GroundandPound.de: Ranks top 10 European male fighters in all divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>MMAViking: Ranks top 5 Scandinavian male fighters in all divisions and Scandinavian female pound for pound.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clothing">Clothing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Clothing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mixed martial arts promotions typically require that male fighters wear shorts in addition to being <a href="/wiki/Barechested" class="mw-redirect" title="Barechested">barechested</a>, thus precluding the use of <a href="/wiki/Keikogi" title="Keikogi">gi</a> or fighting kimono to inhibit or assist <a href="/wiki/Submission_(combat_sport_term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission (combat sport term)">submission</a> holds. Male fighters are required by most athletic commissions to wear groin protectors underneath their trunks.<sup id="cite_ref-njacb_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-njacb-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Female fighters wear <a href="/wiki/Short_shorts" class="mw-redirect" title="Short shorts">short shorts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sports_bra" title="Sports bra">sports bras</a> or other similarly snug-fitting tops. Both male and female fighters are required to wear a <a href="/wiki/Mouthguard" title="Mouthguard">mouthguard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-njacb_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-njacb-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The need for flexibility in the legs combined with durability prompted the creation of various fighting shorts brands, which then spawned a range of <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_clothing" title="Mixed martial arts clothing">mixed martial arts clothing</a> and casual wear available to the public.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fighting_area">Fighting area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Fighting area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the Unified Rules of Mixed Martial Arts, an MMA competition or exhibition may be held in a ring or a fenced area. The fenced area can be round or have at least six sides. Cages vary: some replace the metal fencing with a net, others have a different shape from an octagon, as the term "the Octagon" is trademarked by the UFC (though the 8-sided shape itself is not trademarked).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The fenced area is called a cage generically, or a hexagon, an octagon or an octagon cage, depending on the shape.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed center">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 287.33333333333px"><div style="width: 287.33333333333px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_disciplines">Common disciplines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Common disciplines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Most 'traditional' martial arts have a specific focus and these arts may be trained to improve in that area. Popular disciplines of each type include:<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Stand-up_fighting" title="Stand-up fighting">Stand-up</a></b>: <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">Boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">Kickboxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">Karate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capoeira" title="Capoeira">Capoeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Combat_Sambo" class="mw-redirect" title="Combat Sambo">Combat Sambo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savate" title="Savate">Savate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sanshou" title="Sanshou">Wushu Sanshou</a> are trained to improve stand-up striking.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Clinch_fighting" title="Clinch fighting">Clinch</a></b>: <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">Judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_wrestling" title="Freestyle wrestling">Freestyle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_wrestling" title="Greco-Roman wrestling">Greco-Roman wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art)" title="Sambo (martial art)">Sambo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sanshou" title="Sanshou">Wushu Sanshou</a> are trained to improve <a href="/wiki/Stand-up_grappling_position" class="mw-redirect" title="Stand-up grappling position">clinching</a>, <a href="/wiki/Takedown_(grappling)" title="Takedown (grappling)">takedowns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Throw_(grappling)" title="Throw (grappling)">throws</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> is trained to improve the <a href="/wiki/Strike_(attack)" title="Strike (attack)">striking</a> aspect of the clinch.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Ground_fighting" title="Ground fighting">Ground</a></b>: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Jiu-Jitsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu">Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">Judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art)" title="Sambo (martial art)">Sambo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catch_wrestling" title="Catch wrestling">Catch wrestling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Submission_grappling" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission grappling">submission grappling</a> are trained to improve ground control and position, as well as to achieve <a href="/wiki/Submission_holds" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission holds">submission holds</a>, and defend against them.</li></ul>
<p>Most styles have been adapted from their traditional forms, such as <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> stances, which lack effective counters to leg kicks, the <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> stance, which is poor for defending against takedowns due to its static nature, and <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">Judo</a> or <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Jiu-Jitsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu">Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu</a> techniques, which must be adapted for No <a href="/wiki/Judogi" title="Judogi">Gi</a> competition. It is common for a fighter to train with multiple coaches of different styles or an organized fight team to improve various aspects of their game at once. <a href="/wiki/Aerobic_exercise" title="Aerobic exercise">Cardiovascular conditioning</a>, speed drills, <a href="/wiki/Strength_training" title="Strength training">strength training</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flexibility_(anatomy)" title="Flexibility (anatomy)">flexibility</a> are also important aspects of a fighter's training. Some schools advertise their styles as simply "mixed martial arts", which has become a style in itself, but the training will still often be split into different sections.
</p><p>While mixed martial arts was initially practiced almost exclusively by competitive fighters, this is no longer the case. As the sport has become more mainstream and more widely taught, it has become accessible to wider range of practitioners of all ages. Proponents of this sort of training argue that it is safe for anyone, of any age, with varying levels of competitiveness and fitness.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boxing">Boxing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Boxing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">Boxing</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">Boxing</a> is a combat form that is widely used in MMA and is one of the primary striking bases for many fighters.<sup id="cite_ref-bloodyelbow.com_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloodyelbow.com-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Boxing punches account for the vast majority of strikes during the stand up portion of a bout and also account for the largest number of significant strikes, knock downs and KOs in MMA matches.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Several aspects of boxing are extremely valuable such as footwork, combinations, and defensive techniques like slips, head movement and stance (including chin protection and keeping hands up) commonly known as the Guard position.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Boxing-based fighters have also been shown to throw and land a higher volume of strikes when compared with other striking bases, at a rate of 3.88 per minute with 9.64 per minute thrown (compared with Muay Thai at 3.46 and 7.50, respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-bloodyelbow.com_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloodyelbow.com-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Fighters known for using boxing include <a href="/wiki/Cain_Velasquez" title="Cain Velasquez">Cain Velasquez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Diaz" title="Nick Diaz">Nick Diaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glover_Teixeira" title="Glover Teixeira">Glover Teixeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Junior_dos_Santos" title="Junior dos Santos">Junior dos Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/B.J._Penn" title="B.J. Penn">B.J. Penn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Hardy" title="Dan Hardy">Dan Hardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shane_Carwin" title="Shane Carwin">Shane Carwin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Arlovski" title="Andrei Arlovski">Andrei Arlovski</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Muay_Thai.2FKickboxing"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Muay_Thai/Kickboxing">Muay Thai/Kickboxing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Muay Thai/Kickboxing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">Kickboxing</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> or Thai boxing and <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxing</a>, along with boxing, are recognised as a foundation for striking in mixed martial arts, and are both widely practiced and taught. Although both may seem identical, each has different techniques. Muay Thai originated in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, and is known as the "art of eight limbs", which refers to the use of the legs, knees, elbows and fists.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> One of the primary benefits of training in Muay Thai for MMA is its versatility. Techniques cover the long, middle and short range with everything from kicks to clinch holds and throws.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, kickboxing is a group of stand-up combat martial arts based on kicking and punching. The modern style originated in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and is developed from Karate and Muay Thai. Different governing bodies apply different rules, such as allowing the use of elbows, knees, clinching or throws, etc. Notable fighters who use Muay Thai include former UFC women's strawweight champion <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Jedrzejczyk" class="mw-redirect" title="Joanna Jedrzejczyk">Joanna Jedrzejczyk</a>, UFC Welterweight <a href="/wiki/Darren_Till" title="Darren Till">Darren Till</a> and former UFC champions <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Silva" title="Anderson Silva">Anderson Silva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Aldo" title="José Aldo">José Aldo</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Brazilian_jiu-jitsu_.2F_Grappling"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazilian_jiu-jitsu_/_Grappling">Brazilian jiu-jitsu / Grappling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Brazilian jiu-jitsu / Grappling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_jiu-jitsu" title="Brazilian jiu-jitsu">Brazilian jiu-jitsu</a></div>
<p>Brazilian jiu-jitsu (BJJ) came to international prominence in the martial arts community in the early 1990s, when BJJ expert <a href="/wiki/Royce_Gracie" title="Royce Gracie">Royce Gracie</a> won the <a href="/wiki/UFC_1" title="UFC 1">first</a>, <a href="/wiki/UFC_2" title="UFC 2">second</a> and <a href="/wiki/UFC_4" title="UFC 4">fourth</a> Ultimate Fighting Championships, which at the time were <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">single-elimination</a> martial arts tournaments. Royce often fought against much larger opponents who practiced other styles, including <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shoot-fighting" class="mw-redirect" title="Shoot-fighting">shoot-fighting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a>. It has since become a staple art and key component for many MMA fighters. BJJ and jujutsu are largely credited for bringing widespread attention to the importance of <a href="/wiki/Ground_fighting" title="Ground fighting">ground fighting</a>. BJJ is primarily a ground-based fighting style that emphasizes <a href="/wiki/Joint_lock" title="Joint lock">joint locks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chokehold" title="Chokehold">chokeholds</a>, whereas jujutsu is a method of close combat that utilizes different forms of grappling techniques such as <a href="/wiki/Throw_(grappling)" title="Throw (grappling)">throws</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grappling_hold" title="Grappling hold">holds</a> and joint locks. As jujutsu may also involve the use of a short weapon, it cannot be used to its full potential in mixed martial arts. Current fighters who are known for their BJJ skills include <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_Souza" title="Ronaldo Souza">Ronaldo Souza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glover_Teixeira" title="Glover Teixeira">Glover Teixeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demian_Maia" title="Demian Maia">Demian Maia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fabr%C3%ADcio_Werdum" title="Fabrício Werdum">Fabrício Werdum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Ortega" title="Brian Ortega">Brian Ortega</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judo">Judo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Judo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">Judo</a></div>
<p>Using their knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Ne-waza" class="mw-redirect" title="Ne-waza">ne-waza</a>/ground grappling and <a href="/wiki/Tachi-waza" class="mw-redirect" title="Tachi-waza">tachi-waza</a>/standing grappling, several <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a> practitioners have also competed in mixed martial arts matches.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Fighters who hold a black belt in judo include <a href="/wiki/Fedor_Emelianenko" title="Fedor Emelianenko">Fedor Emelianenko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Silva" title="Anderson Silva">Anderson Silva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dong_Hyun_Kim" title="Dong Hyun Kim">Dong Hyun Kim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cub_Swanson" title="Cub Swanson">Cub Swanson</a>, and Olympians <a href="/wiki/Ronda_Rousey" title="Ronda Rousey">Ronda Rousey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hector_Lombard" class="mw-redirect" title="Hector Lombard">Hector Lombard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Hawn" title="Rick Hawn">Rick Hawn</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hidehiko_Yoshida" title="Hidehiko Yoshida">Hidehiko Yoshida</a>. Former WEC middleweight champion <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Filho" title="Paulo Filho">Paulo Filho</a> has credited judo for his success in an interview.<sup id="cite_ref-Paulo_Filho_Youtube_interview_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paulo_Filho_Youtube_interview-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wrestling">Wrestling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Wrestling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">Wrestling</a></div>
<p>Wrestling (including <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_wrestling" title="Freestyle wrestling">freestyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_wrestling" title="Greco-Roman wrestling">Greco-Roman</a>, and American <a href="/wiki/Folk_wrestling" title="Folk wrestling">folkstyle</a>) gained tremendous respect due to its effectiveness in mixed martial arts competitions. It is widely studied by mixed martial artists and credited for conferring an emphasis on conditioning for explosive movement and stamina, both of which are critical in competitive mixed martial arts. It is known for excellent takedowns, particularly against the legs. Notable wrestlers in MMA include <a href="/wiki/Khabib_Nurmagomedov" title="Khabib Nurmagomedov">Khabib Nurmagomedov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chael_Sonnen" title="Chael Sonnen">Chael Sonnen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Couture" title="Randy Couture">Randy Couture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brock_Lesnar" title="Brock Lesnar">Brock Lesnar</a>, and Olympians <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Cormier" title="Daniel Cormier">Daniel Cormier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Henderson" title="Dan Henderson">Dan Henderson</a>, &amp; gold medalist <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cejudo" title="Henry Cejudo">Henry Cejudo</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Catch-as-catch-can">Catch-as-catch-can</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Catch-as-catch-can">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Catch_wrestling" title="Catch wrestling">Catch wrestling</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Catch_wrestling" title="Catch wrestling">Catch wrestling</a> is the ancestor of freestyle wrestling and includes submissions which are prohibited in freestyle wrestling.<sup id="cite_ref-Catch_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catch-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Widely popular around the world during the 19th and 20th centuries, catch wrestling underwent a decline until it experienced a resurgence with the advent of mixed martial arts in the 90s. The term <i>no holds barred</i> was used originally to describe the wrestling method prevalent in catch wrestling tournaments during the late 19th century wherein no wrestling holds were banned from the competition, regardless of how dangerous they might be. The term was applied to mixed martial arts matches, especially at the advent of the Ultimate Fighting Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A lot of MMA fighters train in catch wrestling as their sole grappling style or as a complement to Brazilian Jiu-jitsu, as it teaches techniques and tactics not found in Brazilian Jiu-jitsu.<sup id="cite_ref-Catch_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catch-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Notable MMA fighters who use catch wrestling as their primary grappling style include <a href="/wiki/Josh_Barnett" title="Josh Barnett">Josh Barnett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Shamrock" title="Ken Shamrock">Ken Shamrock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Shamrock" title="Frank Shamrock">Frank Shamrock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bas_Rutten" title="Bas Rutten">Bas Rutten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazushi_Sakuraba" title="Kazushi Sakuraba">Kazushi Sakuraba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erik_Paulson" title="Erik Paulson">Erik Paulson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minoru_Suzuki" title="Minoru Suzuki">Minoru Suzuki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masakatsu_Funaki" title="Masakatsu Funaki">Masakatsu Funaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rumina_Sato" title="Rumina Sato">Rumina Sato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masakazu_Imanari" title="Masakazu Imanari">Masakazu Imanari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Inoki" title="Antonio Inoki">Antonio Inoki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Sass" title="Paul Sass">Paul Sass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Catch_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catch-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Karate">Karate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Karate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">Karate</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">Karate</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Kyokushin" title="Kyokushin">Kyokushin</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Full_contact_karate" title="Full contact karate">full contact</a> styles, has proven to be effective in the sport as it is one of the core foundations of kickboxing, and specializes in striking techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-karate_UFC_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karate_UFC-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Various styles of karate are practiced by some MMA fighters, notably <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Liddell" title="Chuck Liddell">Chuck Liddell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bas_Rutten" title="Bas Rutten">Bas Rutten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyoto_Machida" title="Lyoto Machida">Lyoto Machida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thompson_(fighter)" title="Stephen Thompson (fighter)">Stephen Thompson</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Makdessi" title="John Makdessi">John Makdessi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uriah_Hall" title="Uriah Hall">Uriah Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Jimmo" title="Ryan Jimmo">Ryan Jimmo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georges_St-Pierre" title="Georges St-Pierre">Georges St-Pierre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyoji_Horiguchi" title="Kyoji Horiguchi">Kyoji Horiguchi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Gaudinot" title="Louis Gaudinot">Louis Gaudinot</a>. Liddell is known to have an extensive striking background in <a href="/wiki/American_Kenpo" title="American Kenpo">Kenpō with Fabio Martella</a><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> whereas <a href="/wiki/Lyoto_Machida" title="Lyoto Machida">Lyoto Machida</a> practices Shotokan Ryu,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and St-Pierre practices <a href="/wiki/Kyokushin" title="Kyokushin">Kyokushin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-knucklepit_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knucklepit-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Taekwondo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a></div>
<p>Several accomplished MMA fighters have an extensive background in taekwondo.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Some fighters who use taekwondo techniques in MMA are former UFC lightweight champion and WEC lightweight champion <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Pettis" title="Anthony Pettis">Anthony Pettis</a>, who is 3rd dan black belt as well as an instructor,<sup id="cite_ref-fightmagazine.com_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fightmagazine.com-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> and former UFC middleweight champion <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Silva" title="Anderson Silva">Anderson Silva</a>, who is 5th dan black belt and still competes in taekwondo.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his instructional book, Anderson Silva admitted the influence of taekwondo in the formation of his unique style. <i>In each of my fights, I tried to utilize techniques from all the various styles I had studied. I threw taekwondo kicks. I threw Muay Thai knees and elbows, and I used my knowledge of Brazilian jiu-jitsu on the ground.</i><sup id="cite_ref-SilvaKrauss2008_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SilvaKrauss2008-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Anthony Pettis has also stated that he is <i>definitely a traditional martial artist first and a mixed martial artist second</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-fightmagazine.com_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fightmagazine.com-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> as well as his <i>style of attacking is different [because of his] taekwondo background.</i><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capoeira">Capoeira</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Capoeira">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Capoeira" title="Capoeira">Capoeira</a></div>
<p>Capoeira has been incorporated into MMA in more recent years and is often used as an addition to Brazilian jiu-jitsu; both originate from Brazil. Several fighters use this martial art when fighting, although not fully, as music and dancing are major components of the discipline. <a href="/wiki/Conor_McGregor" title="Conor McGregor">Conor McGregor</a> incorporated some techniques and has in turn helped Capoeira gain more attention in MMA. It is known for its quick and complex manoeuvres, which use power, speed, and leverage across a wide variety of kicks, spins and techniques.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sambo">Sambo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sambo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art)" title="Sambo (martial art)">Sambo (martial art)</a></div>
<p>Sambo is a Russian martial art, combat sport and self-defense system.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> It is a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">Judo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_Wrestling" class="mw-redirect" title="Freestyle Wrestling">Freestyle Wrestling</a> using a <a href="/wiki/Keikogi" title="Keikogi">Keikogi</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Kurtka" title="Kurtka">Kurtka</a>. Sambo focuses on throwing, takedowns, grappling, and includes submissions from Judo and <a href="/wiki/Catch_Wrestling" class="mw-redirect" title="Catch Wrestling">Catch Wrestling</a>. Sambo also has a modality known as <i>Combat Sambo</i>, which adds punches, kicks, elbows and knees, making it a proto-MMA hybrid fighting style. Sambo is popular in Russia and eastern Europe, where it is taught as a complement to Judo and Wrestling training, Sambo also provides a good base for MMA with all-around skills for combining grappling and striking. Some notable Sambo fighters that transitioned into MMA include: <a href="/wiki/Fedor_Emelianenko" title="Fedor Emelianenko">Fedor Emelianenko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Igor_Vovchanchyn" title="Igor Vovchanchyn">Igor Vovchanchyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Taktarov" title="Oleg Taktarov">Oleg Taktarov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khabib_Nurmagomedov" title="Khabib Nurmagomedov">Khabib Nurmagomedov</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Wushu_Sanshou.2FSanda.2FKung_Fu"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Wushu_Sanshou/Sanda/Kung_Fu">Wushu Sanshou/Sanda/Kung Fu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Wushu Sanshou/Sanda/Kung Fu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sanshou" title="Sanshou">Sanshou</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sanshou" title="Sanshou">Wushu Sanshou</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Chinese_martial_arts" title="Chinese martial arts">Chinese martial arts</a> have also been utilized in MMA. They can be highly effective in competition due to their mixture of striking and takedowns, achieved through a condensation of traditional Chinese martial arts techniques. Most prominent and chief amongst these fighters is <a href="/wiki/Cung_Le" title="Cung Le">Cung Le</a>, who is most notable for his TKO and KO victories over former UFC champions Frank Shamrock (in Strikeforce) and Rich Franklin (at UFC Macau). Other Wushu Sanshou based fighters who have entered MMA include UFC strawweight champion <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Weili" title="Zhang Weili">Zhang Weili</a>, <a href="/wiki/KJ_Noons" class="mw-redirect" title="KJ Noons">KJ Noons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pat_Barry_(fighter)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pat Barry (fighter)">Pat Barry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Tiequan" title="Zhang Tiequan">Zhang Tiequan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Salihov" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim Salihov">Muslim Salihov</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>  and <a href="/wiki/Zabit_Magomedsharipov" title="Zabit Magomedsharipov">Zabit Magomedsharipov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategies">Strategies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Strategies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The techniques utilized in mixed martial arts competition generally fall into two categories: <a href="/wiki/Strike_(attack)" title="Strike (attack)">striking</a> techniques (such as <a href="/wiki/Kick" title="Kick">kicks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knee_(strike)" title="Knee (strike)">knees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punch_(strike)" class="mw-redirect" title="Punch (strike)">punches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elbow_(strike)" title="Elbow (strike)">elbows</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Grappling" title="Grappling">grappling</a> techniques (such as <a href="/wiki/Clinch_hold" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinch hold">clinch holds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pinning_hold" class="mw-redirect" title="Pinning hold">pinning holds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Submission_hold" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission hold">submission holds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweep_(grappling)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweep (grappling)">sweeps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Takedown_(grappling)" title="Takedown (grappling)">takedowns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Throw_(grappling)" title="Throw (grappling)">throws</a>).
</p><p>Today, mixed martial artists must <a href="/wiki/Cross-training" title="Cross-training">cross-train</a> in a variety of styles to counter their opponent's strengths and remain effective in all the phases of combat.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sprawl-and-Brawl">Sprawl-and-Brawl</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sprawl-and-Brawl">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sprawl-and-Brawl is a <a href="/wiki/Stand-up_fighting" title="Stand-up fighting">stand-up fighting</a> tactic that consists of effective stand-up striking, while avoiding <a href="/wiki/Ground_fighting" title="Ground fighting">ground fighting</a>, typically by using <a href="/wiki/Sprawl_(grappling)" title="Sprawl (grappling)">sprawls</a> to defend against <a href="/wiki/Takedown_(grappling)" title="Takedown (grappling)">takedowns</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A Sprawl-and-Brawler is usually a <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxer</a> or <a href="/wiki/Kickbox" class="mw-redirect" title="Kickbox">kickboxer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Thai boxer</a> or <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a> fighter who has trained in various styles of <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, and/or <a href="/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art)" title="Sambo (martial art)">sambo</a> to avoid takedowns to keep the fight standing. This is a form which is heavily practiced in the amateur leagues.
</p><p>These fighters will often study <a href="/wiki/Submission_wrestling" title="Submission wrestling">submission wrestling</a> to avoid being forced into submission should they find themselves on the ground. This style can be deceptively different from traditional kickboxing styles, since sprawl-and-brawlers must adapt their techniques to incorporate <a href="/wiki/Takedown_(grappling)" title="Takedown (grappling)">takedown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ground_fighting" title="Ground fighting">ground fighting</a> defense. A few notable examples are <a href="/wiki/Igor_Vovchanchyn" title="Igor Vovchanchyn">Igor Vovchanchyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mirko_Filipovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirko Filipović">Mirko Filipović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Liddell" title="Chuck Liddell">Chuck Liddell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hunt" title="Mark Hunt">Mark Hunt</a> and more recently <a href="/wiki/Junior_dos_Santos" title="Junior dos Santos">Junior dos Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Arlovski" title="Andrei Arlovski">Andrei Arlovski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Joanna_Jedrzejczyk" class="mw-redirect" title="Joanna Jedrzejczyk">Joanna Jedrzejczyk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground-and-pound">Ground-and-pound</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Ground-and-pound">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ground-and-pound is a strategy consisting of taking an opponent to the ground using a <a href="/wiki/Takedown_(grappling)" title="Takedown (grappling)">takedown</a> or throw, obtaining a top, or <a href="/wiki/Grappling_position" title="Grappling position">dominant grappling position</a>, and then striking the opponent, primarily with fists, <a href="/wiki/Strike_(attack)#Hammerfist" title="Strike (attack)">hammerfists</a>, and elbows. Ground-and-pound is also used as a precursor to attempting <a href="/wiki/Submission_(combat_sport_term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission (combat sport term)">submission</a> holds.
</p><p>The style is used by fighters well-versed in submission defense and skilled at takedowns. They take the fight to the ground, maintain a grappling position, and strike until their opponent submits or is <a href="/wiki/Knockout" title="Knockout">knocked out</a>. Although not a traditional style of striking, the effectiveness and reliability of ground-and-pound has made it a popular tactic. It was first demonstrated as an effective technique by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Coleman" title="Mark Coleman">Mark Coleman</a>, then popularized by fighters such as <a href="/wiki/Chael_Sonnen" title="Chael Sonnen">Chael Sonnen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Frye" title="Don Frye">Don Frye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Trigg" title="Frank Trigg">Frank Trigg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Jones" title="Jon Jones">Jon Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheick_Kongo" title="Cheick Kongo">Cheick Kongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kerr_(fighter)" title="Mark Kerr (fighter)">Mark Kerr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Shamrock" title="Frank Shamrock">Frank Shamrock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tito_Ortiz" title="Tito Ortiz">Tito Ortiz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hughes_(fighter)" title="Matt Hughes (fighter)">Matt Hughes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Weidman" title="Chris Weidman">Chris Weidman</a>, and especially <a href="/wiki/Khabib_Nurmagomedov" title="Khabib Nurmagomedov">Khabib Nurmagomedov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While most fighters use ground-and-pound statically, by way of holding their opponents down and mauling them with short strikes from the top position, a few fighters manage to utilize it dynamically by striking their opponents while changing positions, thus not allowing their opponents to settle once they take them down. <a href="/wiki/Cain_Velasquez" title="Cain Velasquez">Cain Velasquez</a> is one of the most devastating ground strikers in MMA and is known for continuing to strike his opponents on the ground while transitioning between positions.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fedor_Emelianenko" title="Fedor Emelianenko">Fedor Emelianenko</a>, considered among the greatest masters of ground-and-pound in MMA history, was the first to demonstrate this dynamic style of striking in transition. He was striking his opponents on the ground while passing <a href="/wiki/Guard_(grappling)" title="Guard (grappling)">guard</a>, or while his opponents were attempting to recover guard.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the year 2000, MMA play-by-play commentator <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Quadros" title="Stephen Quadros">Stephen Quadros</a> coined the popular phrase <i>lay and pray</i>. This refers to a situation where a wrestler or grappler keeps another fighter pinned or controlled on the mat to avoid a stand up, yet exhibits little urgency to finish the grounded opponent with a knockout or a submission for the majority or entirety of the fight.<sup id="cite_ref-bleacherreport.com_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bleacherreport.com-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The implication of "lay and pray" is that after the wrestler/grappler takes the striker down and 'lays' on him to neutralize the opponent's striking weapons, he 'pray's that the referee does not return them to the standing position. This style is considered by many fans as the most boring style of fighting and is highly criticized for intentionally creating non-action, yet it is effective. Some argue that 'lay-and-pray' is justified and that it is the responsibility of the downed fighter to be able to protect himself from this legitimate fighting technique.<sup id="cite_ref-bleacherreport.com_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bleacherreport.com-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Many consider <a href="/wiki/Jon_Fitch" title="Jon Fitch">Jon Fitch</a>'s style to epitomize 'lay and pray'.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a> Welterweight champion <a href="/wiki/Georges_St-Pierre" title="Georges St-Pierre">Georges St-Pierre</a> has been criticized by fans for playing it safe and applying the lay and pray tactic in his fights,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> as has <a href="/wiki/Bellator_MMA" title="Bellator MMA">Bellator MMA</a> Welterweight champion <a href="/wiki/Ben_Askren" title="Ben Askren">Ben Askren</a>, who justified the tactic, explaining that championship fights are much harder as are five rounds long, compared with the usual three.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Submission-Seeking">Submission-Seeking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Submission-Seeking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Submission-Seeking is a reference to the strategy of taking an opponent to the ground using a takedown or <a href="/wiki/Throw_(grappling)" title="Throw (grappling)">throw</a> and then applying a <a href="/wiki/Submission_hold" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission hold">submission hold</a>, forcing the opponent to <a href="/wiki/Submission_(combat_sport_term)" class="mw-redirect" title="Submission (combat sport term)">submit</a>. While grapplers will often work to attain dominant position, some may be more comfortable fighting from other positions. If a grappler finds themselves unable to force a takedown, they may resort to <i>pulling <a href="/wiki/Guard_(grappling)" title="Guard (grappling)">guard</a></i>, whereby they physically pull their opponent into a dominant position on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Submissions are an essential part of many disciplines, most notably <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Jiu-Jitsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu">Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catch_wrestling" title="Catch wrestling">catch wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sambo_(martial_art)" title="Sambo (martial art)">Sambo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shootwrestling" class="mw-redirect" title="Shootwrestling">shootwrestling</a>. Submission-based styles were popularized in the early UFC events by <a href="/wiki/Royce_Gracie" title="Royce Gracie">Royce Gracie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Shamrock" title="Ken Shamrock">Ken Shamrock</a>, and were the dominant tactic in the early UFCs. Modern proponents of the submission-seeking style, such as <a href="/wiki/Demian_Maia" title="Demian Maia">Demian Maia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_Souza" title="Ronaldo Souza">Ronaldo Souza</a>, tend to come from a <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Jiu-Jitsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu">Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu</a> background.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Score_oriented_fighting">Score oriented fighting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Score oriented fighting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Especially used by fighters with strong <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a> background when facing a highly skilled grappler, or by wrestlers who prefer <a href="/wiki/Stand-up_fighting" title="Stand-up fighting">stand-up fights</a>. Usually fighters who adopt this strategy use takedowns only for <a href="/wiki/Score_(sport)" title="Score (sport)">scoring</a>, allowing the adversary to stand up and continue the fight. They also want to land clear strikes and control the octagon. In order to win the fight by decision all score oriented fighters have to have strong defensive techniques and avoid takedowns.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clinch-Fighting">Clinch-Fighting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Clinch-Fighting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Clinch-Fighting is a tactic consisting of using a <a href="/wiki/Clinch_hold" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinch hold">clinch hold</a> to prevent the opponent from moving away into more distant striking range, while also attempting takedowns and <a href="/wiki/Strike_(attack)" title="Strike (attack)">striking</a> the opponent using <a href="/wiki/Knee_(strike)" title="Knee (strike)">knees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stomp_(strike)" title="Stomp (strike)">stomps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elbow_(strike)" title="Elbow (strike)">elbows</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Punch_(combat)" title="Punch (combat)">punches</a>. The clinch is often utilized by wrestlers and Judokas that have added components of the striking game (typically boxing), and <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> fighters.
</p><p>Wrestlers and Judoka may use clinch fighting as a way to neutralize the superior striking skills of a stand-up fighter or to prevent takedowns by a superior ground fighter. <a href="/wiki/Ronda_Rousey" title="Ronda Rousey">Ronda Rousey</a>, with her <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">Judo</a> background, is considered a master at initiating throws from the clinch to set up <a href="/wiki/Armlock" title="Armlock">armbars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marrocco_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marrocco-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The clinch or "plum" of a <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> fighter is often used to improve the accuracy of <a href="/wiki/Knee_(strike)" title="Knee (strike)">knees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elbow_(strike)" title="Elbow (strike)">elbows</a> by physically controlling the position of the opponent. <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Silva" title="Anderson Silva">Anderson Silva</a> is well known for his devastating Muay Thai clinch. He defeated UFC middle weight champion <a href="/wiki/Rich_Franklin" title="Rich Franklin">Rich Franklin</a> using the Muay Thai clinch and kneeing Franklin repeatedly to the body and face - breaking Franklin's nose. In their rematch Silva repeated this and won again.<sup id="cite_ref-Slack_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slack-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other fighters may use the clinch to push their opponent against the cage or ropes, where they can effectively control their opponent's movement and restrict mobility while striking them with punches to the body or stomps also known as <i>dirty boxing</i> or "Wall and Maul". <a href="/wiki/Randy_Couture" title="Randy Couture">Randy Couture</a> used his <a href="/wiki/Greco_Roman_wrestling" class="mw-redirect" title="Greco Roman wrestling">Greco Roman wrestling</a> background to popularize this style en route to six title reigns in the Ultimate Fighting Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-Sllack_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sllack-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In general, fighters who cannot win fights through lightning offense, or are more suited to win fights in the later rounds or via decision are commonly known as <i>grinders</i>.  Grinders aim to shut down their opponent's game plan and chip away at them via clinching, smothering and ground-and-pound for most of the rounds. Prominent examples of grinders are <a href="/wiki/Pat_Healy_(fighter)" title="Pat Healy (fighter)">Pat Healy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chael_Sonnen" title="Chael Sonnen">Chael Sonnen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Women.27s_mixed_martial_arts"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_mixed_martial_arts">Women's mixed martial arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Women&#039;s mixed martial arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_mixed_martial_arts" title="Women&#39;s mixed martial arts">Women's mixed martial arts</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ronda_Rousey_(11).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ronda_Rousey_%2811%29.JPG/220px-Ronda_Rousey_%2811%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ronda_Rousey_%2811%29.JPG/330px-Ronda_Rousey_%2811%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Ronda_Rousey_%2811%29.JPG/440px-Ronda_Rousey_%2811%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ronda_Rousey_(11).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ronda Rousey; one of the former top Bantamweight fighters</div></div></div>
<p>While mixed martial arts is primarily a male dominated sport, it does have female athletes. Female competition in Japan includes promotions such as the all-female <a href="/wiki/Valkyrie_(mixed_martial_arts)" title="Valkyrie (mixed martial arts)">Valkyrie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jewels_(mixed_martial_arts)" title="Jewels (mixed martial arts)">JEWELS</a> (formerly known as <a href="/wiki/Smackgirl" title="Smackgirl">Smackgirl</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> However historically there has been only a select few major professional mixed martial arts organizations in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> that invite women to compete. Among those are <a href="/wiki/Strikeforce_(mixed_martial_arts)" title="Strikeforce (mixed martial arts)">Strikeforce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellator_Fighting_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellator Fighting Championships">Bellator Fighting Championships</a>, the all female <a href="/wiki/Invicta_Fighting_Championships" title="Invicta Fighting Championships">Invicta Fighting Championships</a>, and the now defunct <a href="/wiki/EliteXC" class="mw-redirect" title="EliteXC">EliteXC</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>There has been a growing awareness of women in mixed martial arts due to popular female fighters and personalities such as <a href="/wiki/Megumi_Fujii" title="Megumi Fujii">Megumi Fujii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miesha_Tate" title="Miesha Tate">Miesha Tate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cristiane_Santos" class="mw-redirect" title="Cristiane Santos">Cristiane "Cyborg" Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronda_Rousey" title="Ronda Rousey">Ronda Rousey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joanna_J%C4%99drzejczyk" title="Joanna Jędrzejczyk">Joanna Jędrzejczyk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holly_Holm" title="Holly Holm">Holly Holm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gina_Carano" title="Gina Carano">Gina Carano</a> among others. Carano became known as "the face of women's MMA" after appearing in a number of <a href="/wiki/EliteXC" class="mw-redirect" title="EliteXC">EliteXC</a> events. This was furthered by her appearances on MGM Television's 2008 revival of their game show <i><a href="/wiki/American_Gladiators_(2008_TV_series)" title="American Gladiators (2008 TV series)">American Gladiators</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Additionally, U.S. Congresswoman <a href="/wiki/Sharice_Davids" title="Sharice Davids">Sharice Davids</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">D</a>-<a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">KS</a>-<a href="/wiki/Kansas%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Kansas&#39;s 3rd congressional district">3</a>), elected in <a href="/wiki/2018_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_Kansas" title="2018 United States House of Representatives elections in Kansas">2018</a>, is a former professional MMA fighter.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Japan, female competition has been documented since the mid-1990s. Influenced by female professional wrestling and <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxing</a>, the Smackgirl competition was formed in 2001 and became the only major all-female promotion in mixed martial arts. Other early successful Japanese female organizations included <a href="/wiki/Ladies_Legend_Pro-Wrestling" title="Ladies Legend Pro-Wrestling">Ladies Legend Pro-Wrestling</a>, ReMix (a predecessor to Smackgirl), U-Top Tournament, K-Grace, and AX.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Aside from all-female organizations, most major Japanese male dominated promotions have held select female competitions. These have included <a href="/wiki/Deep_(mixed_martial_arts)" title="Deep (mixed martial arts)">DEEP</a>, MARS, Gladiator, HEAT, Cage Force, <a href="/wiki/K-1" title="K-1">K-1</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Victory_Road" title="World Victory Road">Sengoku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shooto" title="Shooto">Shooto</a> (under the name G-Shooto), and <a href="/wiki/Pancrase" title="Pancrase">Pancrase</a> (under the name Pancrase Athena).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the United States, prior to the success of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Fighter" title="The Ultimate Fighter">The Ultimate Fighter</a></i> reality show that launched mixed martial arts into the mainstream media,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> there was no major coverage of female competitions. Some early organizations who invited women to compete included, International Fighting Championships, SuperBrawl, <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Cage" title="King of the Cage">King of the Cage</a>, Rage in the Cage, Ring of Combat, Bas Rutten Invitational, and HOOKnSHOOT. From the mid-2000s, more coverage came when organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Strikeforce_(mixed_martial_arts)" title="Strikeforce (mixed martial arts)">Strikeforce</a>, <a href="/wiki/EliteXC" class="mw-redirect" title="EliteXC">EliteXC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellator_Fighting_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellator Fighting Championships">Bellator Fighting Championships</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shark_Fights" title="Shark Fights">Shark Fights</a> invited women to compete.
</p><p>Outside <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, female competition is almost exclusively found in minor local promotions. However, in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> some major organizations have held select female competitions, including <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Showtime_(kickboxing)" title="It&#39;s Showtime (kickboxing)">It's Showtime</a>, Shooto Europe, <a href="/wiki/Cage_Warriors" title="Cage Warriors">Cage Warriors</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M-1_Global" title="M-1 Global">M-1 Global</a>.
</p><p>Following Zuffa's acquisition of Strikeforce in March 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> the UFC began promoting women's fights, with Ronda Rousey rapidly becoming one of the promotion's biggest draws.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Controversy arose in 2013, when CFA (Championship Fighting Alliance) fighter <a href="/wiki/Fallon_Fox" title="Fallon Fox">Fallon Fox</a> came out as a <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> woman. The case became a centerpiece of debates concerning whether it was fair to have a transgender woman compete against <a href="/wiki/Cisgender" title="Cisgender">cisgender</a> women in a contact sport.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Neither the UFC nor Invicta FC says they will allow her to fight, and then-UFC Bantamweight champion Ronda Rousey said she would not fight her.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
