<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Amateur_mixed_martial_arts">Amateur mixed martial arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Amateur mixed martial arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Amateur Mixed Martial Arts is the <a href="/wiki/Amateur_sports" title="Amateur sports">amateur version</a> of the Mixed Martial Arts in which participants engage largely or entirely without remuneration. Under the <a href="/wiki/International_Mixed_Martial_Arts_Federation" title="International Mixed Martial Arts Federation">International Mixed Martial Arts Federation</a> (IMMAF) and World MMA Association (WMMAA), it is practiced within a safe and regulated environment which relies on a fair and objective scoring system and competition procedures similar to those in force in the <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_rules" title="Mixed martial arts rules">professional Mixed Martial Arts rules</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
Amateur MMA is practiced with board shorts and with approved protection gear that includes shin protectors, and amateur <a href="/wiki/MMA_gloves" title="MMA gloves">MMA gloves</a>.
</p><p>The International Mixed Martial Arts Federation and the World Mixed Martial Arts Association announced an amalgamation on 11 April 2018, uniting the two organisations behind one bid for Olympic sport recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Mixed_Martial_Arts_Association">World Mixed Martial Arts Association</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: World Mixed Martial Arts Association">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>World Mixed Martial Arts Association (WMMAA) was founded in 2012 in Monaco by <a href="/wiki/M-1_Global" title="M-1 Global">M-1 Global</a> commercial promoters and is under the leadership of the General Secretary Alexander Endelgarth,  President Finkelstein and Fedor Emelianenko.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The World MMA Association is an organization that manages and develops mixed martial arts, it establishes rules and procedures and hosts MMA competitions.
World MMA Association includes national MMA organizations, representing the sport and registered in accordance with national laws.
</p><p>As of December 2013 WMMAA has 38 member states under its umbrella, in 2017 World MMA Association has 83 members: Afghanistan, Albania, Armenia, Austria, Azerbaijan, Belarus, Belgium, Bulgaria, Canada, Croatia, Colombia, Czech Republic, France, Guatemala, Georgia, Greece, India, Iran, Italy, Kazakhstan, Latvia, Lithuania, Macedonia, Moldova, Monaco, Mongolia, the Netherlands, Poland, Portugal, Romania, Russia, Senegal, Serbia, Slovakia, South Korea, Spain, Switzerland, Tajikistan, Trinidad and Tobago, Turkey, Ukraine, Uzbekistan, Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 20, 2013 the first World MMA Championship was held in Saint Petersburg, Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Mixed_Martial_Arts_Federation">International Mixed Martial Arts Federation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: International Mixed Martial Arts Federation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_Mixed_Martial_Arts_Federation" title="International Mixed Martial Arts Federation">International Mixed Martial Arts Federation</a></div>
<p>On February 29, 2012, the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation (IMMAF) was set up to bring international structure, development and support to mixed martial arts worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> IMMAF launched with support of market leader, the <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">Ultimate Fighting Championship (UFC)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The IMMAF is a non-profit, democratic federation organized according to international federation standards to ensure that MMA as a sport is allowed the same recognition, representation and rights as all other major sports. The IMMAF is registered under Swedish law and is founded on democratic principles, as outlined in their statutes.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> As of March 2015, there are 39 total members from 38<sup id="cite_ref-immaf.org_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immaf.org-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> countries, which come from Austria, Bahrain, Belgium, Brazil, Bulgaria, Cameroon, Canada, Czech Republic, Denmark, El Salvador, Estonia, Finland, France, Germany, Greece, Iceland, India, Ireland (Northern Ireland), Italy, Jordan, Lebanon, Lithuania, Malaysia, Nepal, The Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Pakistan, Paraguay, Poland, Portugal, Romania, The Seychelles, South Africa, Sweden, Switzerland, Tajikistan, Ukraine, the United Kingdom, and the United States of America.<sup id="cite_ref-immaf.org_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immaf.org-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-immaf.org_168-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immaf.org-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-immaf.org_168-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immaf.org-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The IMMAF held its first Amateur World Championships in Las Vegas, USA, from June 30 to July 6, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg/220px-Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg/330px-Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg/440px-Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2640" data-file-height="1980" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Strikeforce_trainer_2010-01-07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A ring-side doctor attends to a fighter following a loss.</div></div></div>
<p>Mixed Martial Arts competitions have changed dramatically since the first Ultimate Fighting
Championship in 1993, specifically with the inception of the <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_rules#Unified_rules" title="Mixed martial arts rules">Unified Rules of Mixed Martial Arts</a>. There remains a paucity of data on injuries that occur in MMA, and resulting concerns with regard to MMA's safety remain. A recent systematic review concluded that the injury incidence rate in MMA appears to be greater than in most, if not all, other popular and commonly practiced combat sports.<sup id="cite_ref-Lystad,_R.P._2014_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lystad,_R.P._2014-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Injury_rates">Injury rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Injury rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a recent meta-analysis of the available injury data in MMA, the injury incidence rate was estimated to be 228.7 injuries per 1000 athlete-exposures (one athlete-exposure is defined as one athlete participating in a single fight).<sup id="cite_ref-Lystad,_R.P._2014_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lystad,_R.P._2014-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The estimated injury incidence rate in MMA is greater than in other full-contact combat sports such as <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a> (44.0 injuries per 1000 athlete-exposures),<sup id="cite_ref-Frey,_A._2004_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frey,_A._2004-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a> (79.4 injuries per 1000 athlete-exposures),<sup id="cite_ref-Lystad,_R.P._2009_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lystad,_R.P._2009-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amateur_boxing" title="Amateur boxing">amateur boxing</a> (77.7 injuries per 1000 athlete-exposures),<sup id="cite_ref-Estwanik,_J.J._1984_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estwanik,_J.J._1984-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Professional_boxing" title="Professional boxing">professional boxing</a> (118.0-250.6 injuries per 1000 athlete-exposures).<sup id="cite_ref-Bledsloe,_G.H._2005_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bledsloe,_G.H._2005-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zazryn,_T.R._2003_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zazryn,_T.R._2003-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zazryn,_T.R._2006_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zazryn,_T.R._2006-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zazryn,_T.R._2009_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zazryn,_T.R._2009-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Injury_pattern">Injury pattern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Injury pattern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In general, the injury pattern in MMA is very similar to that in professional boxing but unlike that found in other combat sports such as judo and taekwondo.<sup id="cite_ref-Lystad,_R.P._2014_172-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lystad,_R.P._2014-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The most commonly injured body region is the head (66.8% to 78.0% of reported injuries) followed by the wrist/hand (6.0% to 12.0% of reported injuries), while the most frequent types of injury were laceration (36.7% to 59.4% of reported injuries), fracture (7.4% to 43.3% of reported injuries), and concussion (3.8% to 20.4% of reported injuries).<sup id="cite_ref-Lystad,_R.P._2014_172-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lystad,_R.P._2014-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The frequency of impact to the ear and low utilization of ear protection leads to a high frequency of perichondral hematoma that can lead to <a href="/wiki/Cauliflower_ear" title="Cauliflower ear">cauliflower ear</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_health">Mental health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Mental health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In preliminary results reported in April 2012 as part of an ongoing study of a 109 professional boxers and MMA fighters being conducted by Dr. Charles Bernick and his colleagues at Cleveland Clinic's Lou Ruvo Center for Brain Health, fighters with more than six years of ring experience were observed to have reductions in size in their hippocampus and thalamus, while fighters with more than twelve years of ring experience were observed to have both reductions in size and symptoms such as memory loss (the hippocampus and thalamus deal with memory and alertness).  Dr. Bernick speculates that the cumulative damage over time from lesser blows may eventually prove an even more important topic of study than that of infrequent concussions.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fatalities">Fatalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Fatalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fatalities_in_mixed_martial_arts_contests" title="Fatalities in mixed martial arts contests">Fatalities in mixed martial arts contests</a></div>
<p>There have been seven known deaths in MMA to date.<sup id="cite_ref-martialhistory_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-martialhistory-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
There were no documented cases of deaths after a sanctioned MMA event prior to 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Houston_Vasquez_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Houston_Vasquez-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2007, there have been six fatalities in mixed martial arts matches. The first was the death of <a href="/wiki/Sam_Vasquez" class="mw-redirect" title="Sam Vasquez">Sam Vasquez</a> on November 30, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Vasquez_death_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vasquez_death-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Vasquez collapsed shortly after being knocked out by Vince Libardi in the third round of an October 20, 2007 fight at the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Center_(Houston)" class="mw-redirect" title="Toyota Center (Houston)">Toyota Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Houston_Vasquez_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Houston_Vasquez-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Vasquez had two separate surgeries to remove blood clots from his brain, and shortly after the second operation suffered a stroke and did not regain consciousness.<sup id="cite_ref-Vasquez_death_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vasquez_death-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The second death stemming from a sanctioned mixed martial arts contest occurred in South Carolina on June 28, 2010, when 30-year-old Michael Kirkham was knocked out and never regained consciousness. He was pronounced dead two days after the fight.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The third death on August 11, 2012 involved 30 year old Tyrone Mims, who was making his amateur MMA debut at “Conflict MMA: Fight Night at the Point VI” in South Carolina, making his the second MMA-related death in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> After being TKO’d in the second round of the fight he became unresponsive and was taken to Medical University Hospital, where he was pronounced dead one hour later. No evidence of brain trauma or concussion was found, however, and the initial autopsy has proved inconclusive. Coroner Rae Wooten explained that his death may likely have been from an irregular heartbeat caused by over exertion; however whether or not his death was a direct result of his fight remains a mystery.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 27, 2014, 29-year-old Booto Guylain was transported to Johannesburg General Hospital to be treated for swelling and bleeding on the brain after suffering a KO loss via elbow in the last round of his fight in South African promotion “Extreme Fighting Championship Africa”. He was unable to make a recovery, and after one week in the hospital he was pronounced dead.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 9, 2016, 28-year-old João Carvalho died following a Total Extreme Fighting event at the National Stadium in Dublin (Ireland). The Portuguese fighter was beaten by TKO, and fell ill twenty minutes after the fight. He was taken immediately to Beaumont hospital, where he underwent emergency brain surgery, but died two days later.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 15, 2017 after a TKO loss resulting from unanswered punches in the second round of his fight, 37 year old Donshay White became unresponsive and collapsed in his locker room and was rushed to the KentuckyOne Health Sts. Mary &amp; Elizabeth Hospital in Kentucky.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> He was soon pronounced dead and was revealed to be caused by hypertensive/atherosclerotic cardiovascular disease.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legality_of_professional_competitions">Legality of professional competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Legality of professional competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_in_Australia" title="Mixed martial arts in Australia">Mixed martial arts in Australia</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_in_Australia" title="Mixed martial arts in Australia">MMA in Australia</a> is permitted in all States and Territories of Australia by various combat sports authorities and organizations. There is debate about the use of the cage, which was banned in <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> and then relegalized in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The cage was banned in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> in March, 2013.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bahrain">Bahrain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Bahrain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MMA is legal in Bahrain. Bahrain National MMA Federation (BNMMAF) has been set up under the patronage of Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Khalid_bin_Hamad_Al_Khalifa" title="Khalid bin Hamad Al Khalifa">Khalid bin Hamad Al Khalifa</a> and the jurisdiction of the Sports Minister Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Nasser_bin_Hamad_Al_Khalifa" title="Nasser bin Hamad Al Khalifa">Nasser bin Hamad Al Khalifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The development of MMA in the nation is convened through KHK MMA, which also owns <a href="/wiki/Brave_Combat_Federation" title="Brave Combat Federation">Brave Combat Federation</a>, which is the largest Mixed Martial Arts promotion in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Bahrain will be hosting World MMA Amateurs Championship 2017 supported by <a href="/wiki/International_Mixed_Martial_Arts_Federation" title="International Mixed Martial Arts Federation">International Mixed Martial Arts Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MMA is tolerated in Belgium but not supported. In May 2012 the Belgian MMA Federation (BMMAF) was accepted by the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation as its third member, after several years of carrying out many of the tasks of a national federation under the former name of the Belgian Shooto and MMA Federation. Active in developing MMA in Belgium from 2005, the group later redefined their activities to include MMA in order to be able to use a cage. Registered as a federation in Belgium in 2006, the former Belgian Shooto and MMA Federation organized more than 1500 MMA bouts (Amateur, B class and A class), and built a structure for the sport nationally that included insurance, rules and regulation, and experience levels for fighters and technical seminars. The BMMAF has continued its activities as part of the wider MMA community under IMMAF.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_in_Brazil" title="Mixed martial arts in Brazil">Mixed martial arts in Brazil</a></div>
<p>January 17, 2013 saw the announcement that the Brazilian MMA Athletic Commission, or Comissao Atletica Brasileira de MMA (CABMMA), had joined the International MMA Federation. The CABMMA represents state federations across Brazil and is spearheaded by lawyers Giovanni Biscardi and Rafael Favettia, a former Executive Secretary of the Minister of Justice and Interim Minister of Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The CABMMA supervised its first event with "UFC on FX 7" on 19 January 2013 at Ibirapuera Gymnasium in São Paulo.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The CABMMA first hit international sports headlines when it suspended fighter Rousimar Palhares for prolonging a submission on opponent Mike Pierce, despite him tapping several times, during <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a> Fight Night 29 in Barueri, Brazil on 9th Oct 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The CABMMA was called to preside over another controversial situation involving a Brazilian competitor, when Vitor Belfort's use of Testosterone Replacement Therapy came to light over <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a> on FX 8 (May 18, 2013)<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Appearing on professional basis around 2008–2009, MMA is a new sport in Bulgaria and growing rapidly. With a strong wrestling and boxing culture in the region, general interest in the sport is huge. However, it remains unregulated. The Bulgarian Federation for Mixed Martial Arts was elected as the national federation representing the Republic of Bulgaria under the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation in October 2014; and like all IMMAF members, is a non-profit, democratic organization. Established in November 2013 by 10 MMA clubs, the organization is headed by UFC competitor Stanislav Nedkov. The federation's registration to the Ministry of Justice was approved in June 2014 and its application for formal recognition by the Ministry of Sport is in its advanced stages.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cambodia">Cambodia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Cambodia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2013, the Cambodian Mixed Martial Arts Association was created under the Cambodian Martial Arts Federation.
At this time there are no MMA events organized with the CMMAA approval. Television channel MYTV holds its KWC promotion under the sanctioning of the Cambodian Boxing Federation, responsible for sanctioning all boxing and <a href="/wiki/Kun_Khmer" class="mw-redirect" title="Kun Khmer">Kun Khmer</a> events in the country, in direct contrast to the situation in neighbouring Thailand.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For many years, professional MMA competitions were illegal in Canada. Section 83(2) of the Canadian Criminal Code deemed that only boxing matches where only fists are used are considered legal.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> However most provinces regulated it by a provincial athletic commission (skirting S. 83(2) by classifying MMA as "mixed boxing"),<sup id="cite_ref-CANL2_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CANL2-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> such as the provinces of Manitoba, Ontario,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, and Northwest Territories. The legality of MMA in the provinces of Alberta, British Columbia, and New Brunswick varies depending on the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-abcboxing.com_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcboxing.com-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Professional MMA competitions remain illegal in the Canadian provinces of Newfoundland and Labrador, Prince Edward Island, Saskatchewan, Yukon, and Nunavut because it is not regulated by an athletic commission.
</p><p>Canada formally decriminalized mixed martial arts with a vote on Bill S-209 on June 5, 2013. The bill formally gives <a href="/wiki/Provinces" class="mw-redirect" title="Provinces">provinces</a> the power to create athletic commissions to regulate and sanction professional mixed martial arts bouts.<sup id="cite_ref-CANL1_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CANL1-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Bill S-209 does not in and of itself make MMA legal across Canada; it allows provinces to make it legal on a province by province basis.<sup id="cite_ref-CANL2_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CANL2-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, the Ranik Ultimate Fighting Federation (<a href="/wiki/Ranik_Ultimate_Fighting_Federation" title="Ranik Ultimate Fighting Federation">RUFF</a>) hosted the first MMA event in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> sanctioned by China's governing body for combat sports, the Wushu Sports Management Center of the General Administration of Sport in China. RUFF formally crowned the first Chinese national MMA champions in 2013 with each champion receiving 1,000,000 RMB in prize money.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Other MMA promotions in China include the 'Real Fight Championship', which has produced three events in <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Denmark, Mixed Martial Arts may be practiced but is not an official or legally regulated sport. On November 11, 2012 the voluntary Danish Mixed Martial Arts Federation held its first official general assembly in Odense, Denmark. There the DMMAF was officially founded and a board was elected headed up by President Claus Larsen. The Federation was publicly launched on Friday November 24, inviting Danish MMA organizations, gyms and academies to sign up as members. The DMMAF is working towards recognition under the Danish Sports Federation, Dansk Idræts Forbund. On November 25 the DMMAF's application to the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation was approved.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There remains political opposition to MMA in France and full contact MMA competition is banned.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> All bouts on French soil recorded as Mixed Martial Arts are in fact held under Pancrase Rules and other variants (Pankration, Kempo, Pankido).<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> These bouts involve no striking on the ground as it is illegal in the country. The Commission National de Mixed Martial Arts (CNMMA) was founded as a non-profit organization for the development of MMA in 2009. The CNMMA had worked over four years to put an educational structure in place, including a technical system for the safe progression from grass-roots level, all the way up to the top professional level.<sup id="cite_ref-cnmma.fr_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnmma.fr-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Comprising 11 regional leagues working under regional technical advisers and teams,<sup id="cite_ref-cnmma.fr_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnmma.fr-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> the CNMMA joined the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation (IMMAF) in March 2013 as The Commission Française de Mixed Martial Arts (CFMMA).<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, CFMMA president <a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Amoussou-Guenou" title="Bertrand Amoussou-Guenou">Bertrand Amoussou</a> ascended to the position of President of the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On June 24, 2019, <a href="/wiki/Roxana_Maracineanu" class="mw-redirect" title="Roxana Maracineanu">Roxana Maracineanu</a>, France's minister of sport announced the legalization of mixed martial arts as of January 1, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ministry of Youth Affairs and Sports (India) has not recognized Mixed Martial Arts as a sport in India. But the sport is growing fast and the Sports Ministry has given direct permission to host events to the biggest and oldest MMA Organization in the country - the <b>All India Mixed Martial Arts Association</b> (AIMMAA).<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> AIMMAA is also the sole representative of the Global Mixed Martial Arts Federation in India.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kumite_1_League" title="Kumite 1 League">Kumite 1 League</a> (K1L) is an innovator in the global MMA industry and the biggest MMA promotion in India. K1L conceptualised a unique 'Country Vs Country' MMA fight format. K1L hosted its first ever 'International Fight&#160;Night' consisting of 13 action-packed 'Team India Vs Team UAE' bouts on the 29th of September 2018 at <a href="/wiki/Sardar_Vallabhbhai_Patel_Indoor_Stadium" title="Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel Indoor Stadium">Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel Indoor Stadium</a>, Mumbai.&#160;Boxing Legend <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a> served as the brand ambassador and mentor for the state-of-the-art league.&#160;K1L is organising 'Warrior Hunt', India's first-ever MMA talent hunt&#160;&amp; Sports Reality TV show in the metro cities of <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a> &amp;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The professional MMA promotion/ league in the country - the <a href="/wiki/Super_Fight_League" title="Super Fight League">Super Fight League</a> is sanctioned by AIMMAA.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The All India Mixed Martial Arts Association is the only MMA Association to have been operating for more than fourteen years in the country, and has organized and promoted many notable events.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> It is the first nation in the world to launch SPORT MMA for younger kids those who are keen on learning the game &amp; participate in the point based championship.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The AIMMAA has more than 20 affiliated member states, working in their respective regions to promote the sport of MMA.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Irish Martial Arts Commission, which is recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sports_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Sports Council">Irish Sports Council</a>, does not include MMA among its recognized martial arts.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Transport,_Tourism_and_Sport" title="Department of Transport, Tourism and Sport">Department of Transport, Tourism and Sport</a> does not recognise MMA as a sport.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2015)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/UFC_Fight_Night:_McGregor_vs._Brandao" title="UFC Fight Night: McGregor vs. Brandao">UFC Fight Night 46</a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Conor_McGregor" title="Conor McGregor">Conor McGregor</a>, was held in Dublin in 2014.
</p><p>Mixed Martial Arts Federation Ireland (MMAFI), intended as a federation for amateur MMA clubs, gained observer status at IMMAF in June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-immaf_mmafi_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immaf_mmafi-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> MMAFI had a meeting in March 2013 with the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Culture,_Arts_and_Leisure_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Department of Culture, Arts and Leisure (Northern Ireland)">Northern Ireland sports minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Car%C3%A1l_N%C3%AD_Chuil%C3%ADn" title="Carál Ní Chuilín">Carál Ní Chuilín</a> about the prospect of getting recognition from <a href="/wiki/Sport_Northern_Ireland" title="Sport Northern Ireland">Sport Northern Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-immaf_mmafi_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immaf_mmafi-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_in_Japan" title="Mixed martial arts in Japan">Mixed martial arts in Japan</a></div>
<p>MMA competition has been legal in Japan since at least the mid-1980s, when <a href="/wiki/Pancrase" title="Pancrase">Pancrase</a> fights began to be held. There are several MMA-related organizations, including <a href="/wiki/Rizin_Fighting_Federation" title="Rizin Fighting Federation">RIZIN FF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deep_(mixed_martial_arts)" title="Deep (mixed martial arts)">DEEP</a>, Pancrase,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shooto" title="Shooto">Shooto</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Fighting Nexus,<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Deep,<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Grachan<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/ZST" title="ZST">ZST</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2013 the Malaysia Mixed Martial Arts Association (MASMMAA) was formally announced as the official national governing body for MMA in Malaysia, ahead of its formation in December 2013. MASMMAA is registered under the Malaysian Sports Development Act 1997 and recognized by the Commissioner of Sports, under the auspices of the office of the Youth &amp; Sports Ministry. The federation comprises representatives of ten states out of fourteen in Malaysia. MASMMAA became affiliated to the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation in April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-mmauncagedmag.com_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmauncagedmag.com-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Norway, professional MMA is illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Since 1981, all sports involving knockouts as a method of victory were banned but it was lifted for professional boxing in late 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Norwegian MMA fighters must therefore travel abroad to compete. The Norwegian MMA Federation (NMMAF) was elected as a full member of the International MMA Federation (IMMAF) on 22 April 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> representing 49 member gyms across Norway.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012 the "Merkekamper" concept was introduced by the NMMAF, with government sanctioning, which enables member MMA gyms to hold events with sparring matches, but governed by strict rules concerning how hard a fighter is permitted to strike.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 April 2019, MMA was recognized by and welcomed into the Norwegian Martial Arts Federation (<a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> <i>Kampsportforbundet</i>), a federation of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Olympic_and_Paralympic_Committee_and_Confederation_of_Sports" title="Norwegian Olympic and Paralympic Committee and Confederation of Sports">Norwegian Olympic and Paralympic Committee and Confederation of Sports</a> (NIF) with the goal of growing the amaeteur sport.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mixed_Martial_Arts_Pakistan" title="Mixed Martial Arts Pakistan">Mixed Martial Arts Pakistan</a> organizes MMA events. The organization was founded in 2007 by veteran Pakistani MMA fighter <a href="/wiki/Bashir_Ahmad_(mixed_martial_artist)" title="Bashir Ahmad (mixed martial artist)">Bashir Ahmad</a> for promotion of MMA in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The FMMAP is recognized by the Portuguese government as a non-profit sports federation and oversees Amateur MMA competition and coaching nationally. Based in Vila do Conde, the Federação de Mixed Martial Arts de Portugal (FMMAP) was founded as a collaborative effort between six existing non-profit organizations in 2012, as Portugal's first dedicated MMA Federation. This is in line with government requirements for all sport federations in Portugal which stipulates that they consist of at least three associated, non-profit groups. The composite FMMAP organisations are all involved in the coaching and promotion of MMA with a shared goal for the amateur sport, but come from various martial arts that include Karate, Kickboxing, Muay Thai, Pankration Athlima, Mixed Martial Arts, Jeet Kune Do, Freestyle martial arts, Brazilian Jiu-Jitsu and Wrestling. Affiliated groups at launch were AAMU - Associação Artes Marciais, Associação de Artes Marciais e Desportos de Combate (Açores), Associação Areagon (Chaves City), Associação Mirandelense de Artes Orientais (Mirandela City), Associação Portuguesa de Ciências de Combate/JKD Unlimited Portugal (Lisbon City), KMD MMA system (Porto City), Barcelos Gym (Barcelos City). The FMMAP is affiliated to the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation (IMMAF).<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Romanian Mixed Martial Arts Federation (RMMAF) was established in 2012 as a legal non-profit federation under the Ministry of Youth and Sport in Romania. The Federation was formed by the board of MMA organization AGON and backed by a broad representation of the Romanian MMA community, including around twenty MMA clubs and non-profit MMA organizations around the country. Based in Bucharest, Romania AGON club was founded in its present legal form in June 2012, following a long period of time of acting under different other organisations, with Gheorghe Stanciu elected as its president. The RMMAF is affiliated to the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation (IMMAF).<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 2012, MMA was given 'National Sport' status in Russia, and on the same day fighter and <a href="/wiki/M-1_Global" title="M-1 Global">M-1 Global</a> promoter <a href="/wiki/Fedor_Emelianenko" title="Fedor Emelianenko">Fedor Emelianenko</a> was appointed to the role of Russian MMA Union president.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The MMA program at Singapore is licensed by the Cantonment Police Division.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MMA competition is legal<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> and under the purview of the Swedish Mixed Martial Arts Federation (SMMAF), which was formed in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> and began overseeing MMA events and governing the sport as a whole in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-SWEDENBL_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SWEDENBL-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> In 2009 the SMMAF was accepted into the Association of Swedish Budo and Martial Arts Federation,<sup id="cite_ref-SWEDENBL_268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SWEDENBL-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> thus granting MMA "national sport" status and making its approved clubs eligible for partial government subsidization.<sup id="cite_ref-SWEDENBL_268-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SWEDENBL-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> On April 30, 2011, the SMMAF sanctioned the first event under its purview to utilize the <a href="/wiki/Unified_Rules_of_Mixed_Martial_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Rules of Mixed Martial Arts">Unified Rules of Mixed Martial Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> The Swedish Mixed Martial Arts Federation governs the sport of MMA in Sweden as a member affiliated to the International Mixed Martial Arts Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-immaf.org_168-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immaf.org-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The SMMAF hit the headlines when it withdrew Swedish headliner, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Gustafsson" title="Alexander Gustafsson">Alexander Gustafsson</a>, from competing at <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a> on FUEL 9 in Sweden (April 6, 2013), due to a facial laceration.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MMA competition is legal and under the purview of the Professional Mixed Martial Arts Council or PROMMA Africa,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> which was formed in 2010 with the main purpose to regulate MMA at larger MMA promotions such as EFC Worldwide (Formerly known as EFC Africa). PROMMA Africa began overseeing Rise of the Warrior MMA events in 2010. In 2012 the PROMMA Africa Council was accepted into the Mixed Martial Arts Association of South Africa (MASA) thus granting MMA "national sport" status.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In addition to EFC Africa, there are other leagues such as Dragon Legends MMA.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MMA is officially sanctioned by the government and sports authorities of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwanese</a> MMA fighters are currently training and competing at international level, with several in the <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultimate Fighting Championships">UFC</a> and other MMA organizations. Many major international MMA fights are held at stadiums in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> every year. Additionally, many martial arts schools and gyms in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> provide professional level MMA training.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Sports_Authority_of_Thailand" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports Authority of Thailand">Sports Authority of Thailand</a> banned competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> It has been speculated that the <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a> industry played a factor in the Sports Authority of Thailand (SAT)'s final decision, as MMA could potentially take away business from Muay Thai.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> SAT Deputy Governor Sakol Wannapong has said "Organizing a MMA event here would hurt the image of Muay Thai, if you want to do this kind of business, you should do it in another country. Organizing MMA here could mislead the public into believing that Muay Thai is brutal."
</p><p>Jussi Saloranta, the owner of Thailand's only MMA promotion, DARE Fight Sports, revealed that his lawyers found that the ban was actually premature, and that from a legal standpoint, there is no law banning mixed martial arts in the country, suggesting that the SAT's ban was more of a scare tactic. DARE continue to showcase events, informing fans only at the last minute through texts on the day of the event, and presenting the videos on YouTube as <i>The Most Dangerous Gameshow</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> Saloranta has also helped set up the MMA Association of Thailand, in the hopes of reaching a compromise with SAT and regulating mixed martial arts in Thailand.
</p><p>On September 12, 2013, DARE Fight Sports released a statement announcing SAT had removed the ban on MMA and would henceforth sanction the sport in Thailand.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dare Fight Sports is currently the only MMA organization in Thailand to be officially sanctioned and publicized by the <a href="/wiki/Tourism_authority_of_Thailand" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourism authority of Thailand">tourism authority of Thailand</a>, although there are new MMA organizations appearing around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mixed_martial_arts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts_in_the_United_States" title="Mixed martial arts in the United States">Mixed martial arts in the United States</a></div>
<p>In the United States, professional MMA is overseen by the Association of Boxing Commissions.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> According to the Associations of Boxing Commissions, professional MMA competitions are allowed in all states.<sup id="cite_ref-abcboxing.com_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcboxing.com-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Alaska has no boxing or athletic commission. Montana has a state athletic commission, although it does not regulate MMA. However, MMA is legal in both states. West Virginia became the 44th state to regulate mixed martial arts on March 24, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> On March 8, 2012, Wyoming became the 45th state to regulate MMA.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> On May 4, 2012, it was announced that Vermont had become the 46th state to regulate MMA.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Legislation allowing MMA in Connecticut came into effect on October 1, 2013, making it the 47th state to regulate the sport.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> On March 22, 2016, the New York State Assembly voted to lift the State's 1997 ban on MMA and on April 14, 2016 Governor Cuomo signed the bill legalizing and regulating the sport into law.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
